128383 6Selects the GPIB bus on which to perform the operation.  The VI addresses the interface indicated by bus as a Listener.  If you have only one GPIB interface in your computer, the default bus number is 0. For additional GPIB interfaces, see the software installation instructions included with your GPIB board.
128698 Termination mode specifies how the GPIB driver should determine when the read is finished.  All values from 0-255 (0x0-0xFF) will be taken to be an eos byte which wll stop the read when it is recieved in the data stream or when end is detected.  STOPend 256 (0x100) (the default) indicates to stop the read when end is detected.  The read  will always stop when the requested count has been read.
129098 status is a Boolean array in which each bit describes a state of the GPIB Controller. If an error occurs, the GPIB VIs set bit 15. GPIB error is valid only if bit 15 of status is set.
129282 GPIB status vector:
129303 status[0] - Device Clear State
129334  status[1] - Device Trigger State
129368  status[2] - Listener Active State
129404 status[3] - Talker Active State
129437 status[4] - Attention line asserted
129474 status[5] -
129486 Controller In Charge
129507  status[6] - Remote State
129533  status[7] - Lockout State
129561 status[8] - I/O Completed 
129589 status[9] - not used
129610  status[10]- not used
129632  status[11]- not used
129655 status[12]- SRQ line asserted when CIC
129695 status[13]- EOI or EOS detected
129727  status[14]- Timeout occured
129756  status[15]- GPIB error detected
129792 GPIB error is valid only if bit 15 of status is set.
129845 GPIB Error:
129862 -No error
129877 -Function requires GPIB to be CIC
129916 -No listeners detected on write
129953 -Controller not addressed correctly
129994 -Invalid argument(s)
130021 (perhaps bad address string????)
130059 -Function requires GPIB to be SC
130097 -I/O operation aborted
130125 -hardware not present
130152 -DMA error
130168 -DMA bus timeout
130190 -New I/O attempted while I/O in 
130229 progress
130243 -function not implemented
130274 -file system error
130298 -shareable board exclusively owned
130338 -GPIB bus error (commands)
130370 -Serial Poll Byte Lost
130398 -SRQ line cannot be cleared
130431 -Unrecognized commandEAbyte count refers to the number of bytes that pass over the GPIB.
130521 This integer represents a GPIB address.  The low byte is the primary GPIB address (0-30) and the high byte is either 0 or a secondary GPIB address (96-126 or 0x60-0x7E).  Use MakeAddress.vi to construct a GPIB address which uses secondary addressing.RNcount. The VI returns up to count data bytes from the device in data string. 
130855 GPIB status vector:
130876 status[0] - Device Clear State
130907  status[1] - Device Trigger State
130941  status[2] - Listener Active State
130977 status[3] - Talker Active State
131010 status[4] - Attention line asserted
131047 status[5] -
131059 Controller In Charge
131080  status[6] - Remote State
131106  status[7] - Lockout State
131134 status[8] - I/O Completed 
131162 status[9] - not used
131183  status[10]- not used
131205  status[11]- not used
131228 status[12]- SRQ line asserted when CIC

187705 GPIB error is valid only if bit 15 of status is set. 
187759 GPIB Error:
187776 -No error

187830 -No listeners detected on write

188345 -Unrecognized commandEAbyte count refers to the number of bytes that pass over the GPIB.
188437 status is a Boolean array in which each bit describes a state of the GPIB Controller. If an error occurs, the GPIB VIs set bit 15. GPIB error is valid only if bit 15 of status is set.
188621 GPIB status vector:
188642 status[0] - Device Clear State
188673  status[1] - Device Trigger State
188707  status[2] - Listener Active State
188743 status[3] - Talker Active State
188776 status[4] - Attention line asserted
188813 status[5] -
188825 Controller In Charge
188846  status[6] - Remote State
188872  status[7] - Lockout State
188900 status[8] - I/O Completed 
188928 status[9] - not used
188949  status[10]- not used
188971  status[11]- not used
188994 status[12]- SRQ line asserted when CIC
189034 status[13]- EOI or EOS detected
189066  status[14]- Timeout occured
189095  status[15]- GPIB error detected
189129 This integer represents a GPIB address.  The low byte is the primary GPIB address (0-30) and the high byte is either 0 or a secondary GPIB address (96-126 or 0x60-0x7E).  Use MakeAddress.vi to construct a GPIB address which uses secondary addressing.
189382 3Selects the GPIB bus on which to perform the operation.  The VI addresses the interface indicated by bus as a Talker. If you have only one GPIB interface in your computer, the default bus number is 0. For additional GPIB interfaces, see the software installation instructions included with your GPIB board.
189692 The end of transfer mode describes the method of signaling the end of the data to the listener.  Its values are:
189805   2 (default) DABend - Send eoi with last byte.
189853  1 NL end - Send linefeed with eoi after data.
189900  0 NULLend - Do nothing at end of transfer.OKdata string contains the data bytes that the VI sends to the GPIB device. 
190024 GPIB status vector:
190045 status[0] - Device Clear State
190076  status[1] - Device Trigger State
190110  status[2] - Listener Active State
190146 status[3] - Talker Active State
190179 status[4] - Attention line asserted
190216 status[5] -
190228 Controller In Charge

190275  status[7] - Lockout State
190303 status[8] - I/O Completed

294283 Instr Error Out Cluster.ctl
295255 <wwww
295856 RSRC
295863 LVCCLBVW*
295874 | *`
295882 (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram.  The error out cluster contains the following parameters: 
296227      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.

447293 f(cluster) error in:  a cluster describing any error conditions prior to this VI's execution.  The default input of this cluster is no error.  If an error has already occurred, this VI does nothing.  The error in cluster contains the following parameters: 
447551      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
447602      If status is TRUE, this VI does nothing.
447649      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
447707      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
447764      error, and a positive value is a warning.
447812      (ABC) source:  an indication of where an 
447859      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
447908 ZV(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred. If status is TRUE, this VI does nothing.
448000 (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram.  The error out cluster contains the following parameters: 
448345      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
448397      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
448455      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
448512      error, and a positive value is a warning.
448560      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
448610      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
448662 no error

478618 /Primary GPIB address ranging from 0 to 30.  Used to form the low order byte of the GPIB address which will be accepted by 488.2 functions.  The value of 31 (default) means return the NOADDR constant (0xFFFF) as the packed address.  The VI places primary address in the lower byte of the packed address.
478926 Secondary GPIB address ranging from 0 to 30.  Used to form the high order byte of the GPIB address which will be accepted by 488.2 functions. The value of 31 (default) means use no secondary address. The VI places secondary address in the upper byte of the packed address.
479202 VThis integer represents a GPIB address.  The low byte is the primary GPIB address (0-30) and the high byte is either 0 or a secondary GPIB address (96-126 or 0x60-0x7E).  packed address contains primary address in its lower byte and secondary address in its upper byte. You can use packed address as the address input to the GPIB 488.2 VIs. 
479547 True if either primary or secondary addresses are outside ot the range 0-31.  address error indicates whether a range error has occurred.

490780 Initializes the software connection to the instrument.  In the case of VXI instruments controlled via NI-VXI, initializes the NI-VXI library, reads in the resource manager table, calculates A16 configuration addresses, determines memory requirements, and stores base addresses into A24 or A32 space.  For VXI instruments controlled via GPIB-VXI, performs all of the above except initialization of NI-VXI libraries.  You must run the INSTR Close VI once for every time you run this VI.

523973 A unique reference to an instrument I/O session.  It identifies which device to communicate with and all configuration information to perform the I/O.  An instr handle is returned from the Instr Open VI or the Initialize VI of an instrument driver.
524225 (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram.  The error out cluster contains the following parameters: 
524570      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
524622      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
524680      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
524737      error, and a positive value is a warning.
524785      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
524835      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
524884 [W(string) source:  an indication of where an error occurred, usually the name of the VI.1-(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred."

634881 instr vtl global
635186 Initializes the software connection to the instrument.  In the case of VXI instruments controlled via NI-VXI, initializes the NI-VXI library, reads in the resource manager table, calculates A16 configuration addresses, determines memory requirements, and stores base addresses into A24 or A32 space.  For VXI instruments controlled via GPIB-VXI, performs all of the above except initialization of NI-VXI libraries.  You must run the INSTR Close VI once for every time you run this VI.$

675127 A unique reference to an instrument I/O session.  It identifies which device to communicate with and all configuration information to perform the I/O.  An instr handle is returned from the Instr Open VI or the Initialize VI of an instrument driver.
675379 (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram.  The error out cluster contains the following parameters: 
675724      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
675776      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
675834      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
675891      error, and a positive value is a warning.
675939      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
675989      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.

784835 (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram.  The error out cluster contains the following parameters: 
785180      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
785232      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
785290      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
785347      error, and a positive value is a warning.
785395      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
785445      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
785494 [W(string) source:  an indication of where an error occurred, usually the name of the VI.1-(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
785634 (ABC) Uniquely identifies the instrument to establish communications with.  The grammar for the instrument descriptor is shown below.  Parameters are shown in lower-case and optional parameters are shown in square brackets ([]).
785864 GPIB:   INSTR{GPIB[bd]::prim addr[::sec addr]}
785911 VXI:  INSTR{VXI::logical addr}
785942 GPIB-VXI:   INSTR{GPIB-VXI[bd]::logical addr[prim addr]}
786000 Optional Parameter Default Values:
786035     bd - GPIB board (0)
786059     prim addr - GPIB primary address (1)
786100     sec addr - GPIB secondary address (none)
786145     logical addr - VXI logical address 
786186 EXAMPLE:  A GPIB instrument on GPIB board 0, at primary address 5, and no secondary addressing.
786284 INSTR{GPIB::5}"

786332 (ABC) 
786339 The name of the VI that is calling this VI.  If an error occurs during the operation of this VI, the value in source will be placed in the source element of the error out cluster. 
786522 (I32) 
786529 A unique reference to an instrument I/O session.  It identifies which device to communicate with and all configuration information to perform the I/O.  An instr handle is returned from the Instr Open VI or the Initialize VI of an instrument driver.
786780 f(cluster) error in:  a cluster describing any error conditions prior to this VI's execution.  The default input of this cluster is no error.  If an error has already occurred, this VI does nothing.  The error in cluster contains the following parameters: 
787038      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
787089      If status is TRUE, this VI does nothing.

787194      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
787251      error, and a positive value is a warning.
787299      (ABC) source:  an indication of where an 
787346      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
787395 ZV(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred. If status is TRUE, this VI does nothing."

865158 84(u32) task ID: identifies the group and I/O pattern.D@(u32) pattern: specifies the new state of the lines in the port.
865281 x(i32) line mask: determines which lines in the port the write affects. If you set line mask to -1, the VI writes to the entire port and sets all the lines in the port to the states specified by the bits in pattern. If you set only bit n in line mask, the VI changes only line n in the port to the state that bit n of pattern specifies. The default setting for line mask is -1.51(u32) task ID out: has the same value as task ID.

892165 (i32) line mask: determines which lines this VI reads. If you set line mask to -1 (all ones), the VI reads the entire port. If you set only bit n in line mask, the VI reads only line n of the port. If the state of line n is high, the VI sets bit n of pattern. The VI sets to 0 the bits of pattern that correspond to lines the VI has not read. The default setting for line mask is -1 which is shown as all ones since the binary representation is the default selection.62(u32) pattern: the data the VI read from the port.51(u32) task ID out: has the same value as task ID.

920729 gc(i16) device: the device number you assigned to the data acquisition device when you configured it.
920833 /(i16) port width: the total width in bits of the port. For example, you can combine two 4-bit ports into an 8-bit port on an MIO board by setting port width to 8.
920998 When port width is greater than the physical port width of a digital port, the following restrictions apply. The port width must be an integral multiple of the physical port width, and the port numbers in the combined port must begin with the port named by port number and must increase consecutively. For example, if port  number is 3 and port width is 24 (bits), the VI uses ports 3, 4, and 5.
921396 ?(i32) line direction map: specifies the direction of each line in the port. If a bit is 0 in the line map, the line is an input line. If a bit is 1, the line is an output line. Setting line direction map to -1 makes all the lines in a port output lines. Setting line direction map to 0 makes all the lines in a port input lines. Except for the NB-TIO-10 and PC-TIO-10, this is how you must use line direction map. The NB-TIO-10 and PC-TIO-10 are the only boards on which you can configure lines within a port for different directions. The default for line direction map is 0.
921974 (u32) task ID: uniquely identifies the group. You use this value as the task ID to refer to this group in subsequent digital port VI calls.
922117 (cluster) error in:  a cluster describing any error conditions prior to this VI's execution.  The default input of this cluster is no error.  The error in cluster contains the following parameters: 
922317      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
922369      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
922427      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an 
922485      error, and a positive value is a warning.
922533      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
922583      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
922632 xt(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred. Regardless of the value of status, this VI clears the input operation.
922753 D(string) port number: specifies the port this VI configures. A port number value of 0 signifies port 0, a port number of 1 signifies port 1, and so on. If you use an SCXI-1160, SCXI-1161, SCXI-1162, or SCXI-1163 module, use the SCx!MDy syntax, where x is the chassis and y is the module device number, to specify the module."
923081 no error
923090 ERROR
923096 no error
923105 ERROR
923112 (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.  A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an error, and a positive value is a warning.[W(string) source:  an indication of where an error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
923352 (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram.  The error out cluster contains the following parameters: 
923697      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
923749      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.

923865      error, and a positive value is a warning.

945135 1This error handler is used primarily to inform the user if an input error exists, to describe the error, and to identify where it occurred.  The information for this is derived from the inputs error in, error code, and error source, and from an internal error description table.  The table describes all errors that can be created by LabVIEW or its associated I/O operations.  The handler has provisions to take alternative actions, such as to cancel or set an error status, and to test for and describe user-defined errors.  See instruction on the front panel.

969134 HDcode out is the error code indicated by the error in or error code.
969207 no error
969216 ERROR
969222 no error
969231 ERROR
969239 =type of dialog determines what type dialog box will be displayed, if any. Regardless of its value, the VI outputs error information and message describing the error.
969410 displays no dialog box. This is useful if you want to have programmatic control over how the error is handled.
969525 (the default value) displays a dialog box with a single OK button. After the user responds, the VI returns control to the main VI.
969660 displays a dialog box with buttons allowing the user to either continue or stop. If the user cancels, the VI calls the Stop function to halt execution. 
969816 no dialog
969826 OK message
969837 continue or stop message
969865 exception action is a way for you to create exceptions to error handling. You can treat what is normally an error as no error, or treat a no error condition as an error using this parameter. 
970061 (the default value) performs no error exception handling. 
970124 cancels error under the following conditions:
970172 If the VI detects an error, as described in the status and error code parameters, and if that error code value matches exception code and the error source value matches exception source, the VI sets status out to FALSE, code out to 0, and source out to an empty string. An empty exception source string matches any error source string.
970512 sets error under the following conditions:
970557 If the VI detects no error, as described in the status and error code parameters, but the code value of error in matches exception code and the error source value matches exception source, the VI sets status out to TRUE, code out to the code value from error in, and source out to the source value from error in.
970870 b^exception code is the error code that you want to treat as an exception. By default, it is 0.
970968 error code is a numeric error code. If error in indicates an error, the VI ignores error code. If not, the VI tests it. A non-zero value signifies an error.
971127 no exception
971141 cancel error on match
971163 set error on match
971183 user-defined codes is an array of the numeric error codes you define in your VIs. The VI searches this array after searching the internal list of error codes. Codes in the range of 5000 to 9999 are reserved for users.
971403 user-defined descriptions is an array of descriptions of user-defined codes. If an incoming error matches one in user-defined codes, the VI uses the corresponding description from user-defined descriptions in message.
971621 2.source out indicates the source of the error.
971669 }yexception source is the error message that you want to use to test for an exception. By default, it is an empty string. 
971794 error source is an optional string you can use to describe the source of error code. The VI uses the string in message if there is an error.
971935 jferror in describes an error that you want to check. If unwired, this VI checks error code for errors.
972041 status is TRUE if an error occurred. If this value is FALSE, then the error handler assumes that no error occurred according to the error in, and then checks the error code.

1021966 error codes (hidden)
1022297 1This error handler is used primarily to inform the user if an input error exists, to describe the error, and to identify where it occurred.  The information for this is derived from the inputs error in, error code, and error source, and from an internal error description table.  The table describes all errors that can be created by LabVIEW or its associated I/O operations.  The handler has provisions to take alternative actions, such as to cancel or set an error status, and to test for and describe user-defined errors.  See instruction on the front panel.

1024452 . Interpret it bit-wise as follows: x4000: serial port VI error; x0001: receiving queue overflowed or character was received after end-of-file character; x0002: character was lost by overwrite; x0004: parity error; x0008: framing error; x0010: break condition; x0020: CTS timeout; x0040:  DSR timeout; x0080: RLSD timeout; x0100: transmission queue was full when new character arrived; x0200: parallel device timeout; x0400: parallel device I/O error; x0800: parallel device not selected; x1000: parallel device out of paper; x8000: requested mode is  not supported or the idComDev parameter is invalid.  Consult the LabVIEW serial port manual for more information.SD
1025136 message
1025259  INSTRUCTIONS:
1025275 Normal Use:  When using subVIs that incorporate the error in/error out (or error I/O) structure, place this handler where you want to inform the user of an error, typically at the end of the I/O data path, as the last action of the program.  If the error in status is ERROR, the handler creates a message describing the error and its source.  If the type of dialog = 1 (default), the message is displayed to the user, who can only acknowedge it.  If the type = 2, the user can acknowledge the message or abort execution; aborting a program with active I/O is not recommended.  If the type = 0, no message is displayed; this is used to process the error programmatically, and the error out cluster elements are wired to individual terminals for that reason.  
1026035 Other Uses:
1026049 local testing.  To test the error code of a subVI or function that does not have the error I/O structure, you can wire its error code and a source string to the local error code and error source inputs.  If error in status indicates no error and error code is not equal to 0, the local code and source are substituted for the error in values, and the status is set TRUE (ERROR).
1026429 user-defined codes.  The error handler has tables of error codes and descriptions for all LabVIEW I/O operations (file, GPIB, DAQ, etc.).  You can augment the tables with the user-defined arrays.  Codes from 5000 to 9999 are reserved for user assignments.
1026686 exception handling.  This mechanism is available either to set the error out status FALSE on what is normally an error or to set the status TRUE on what is normally not an error.  If exception action > 0, the error in code and source are checked.  If they match the exception code and source, the error out status is adjusted accordingly.  That is, if the action = 1, the error out status is set to FALSE and code is set to zero and if the action = 2, the error out is set to TRUE and the code is unchanged.  An empty exception source matches any error in source.  H

1071869  INSTRUCTIONS:
1071885 Normal Use:  When using subVIs that incorporate the error in/error out (or error I/O) structure, place this handler where you want to inform the user of an error, typically at the end of the I/O data path, as the last action of the program.  If the error in status is ERROR, the handler creates a message describing the error and its source.  If the type of dialog = 1 (default), the message is displayed to the user, who can only acknowedge it.  If the type = 2, the user can acknowledge the message or abort execution; aborting a program with active I/O is not recommended.  If the type = 0, no message is displayed; this is used to process the error programmatically, and the error out cluster elements are wired to individual terminals for that reason.  
1072645 Other Uses:
1072659 local testing.  To test the error code of a subVI or function that does not have the error I/O structure, you can wire its error code and a source string to the local error code and error source inputs.  If error in status indicates no error and error code is not equal to 0, the local code and source are substituted for the error in values, and the status is set TRUE (ERROR).
1073039 user-defined codes.  The error handler has tables of error codes and descriptions for all LabVIEW I/O operations (file, GPIB, DAQ, etc.).  You can augment the tables with the user-defined arrays.  Codes from 5000 to 9999 are reserved for user assignments.
1073296 exception handling.  This mechanism is available either to set the error out status FALSE on what is normally an error or to set the status TRUE on what is normally not an error.  If exception action > 0, the error in code and source are checked.  If they match the exception code and source, the error out status is adjusted accordingly.  That is, if the action = 1, the error out status is set to FALSE and code is set to zero and if the action = 2, the error out is set to TRUE and the code is unchanged.  An empty exception source matches any error in source.  
1073863 . Interpret it bit-wise as follows: x4000: serial port VI error; x0001: receiving queue overflowed or character was received after end-of-file character; x0002: character was lost by overwrite; x0004: parity error; x0008: framing error; x0010: break condition; x0020: CTS timeout; x0040:  DSR timeout; x0080: RLSD timeout; x0100: transmission queue was full when new character arrived; x0200: parallel device timeout; x0400: parallel device I/O error; x0800: parallel device not selected; x1000: parallel device out of paper; x8000: requested mode is  not supported or the idComDev parameter is invalid.  Consult the LabVIEW serial port manual for more information.

1078683 The Write to Digital Port VI outputs a pattern (in binary) to a specified digital port.  
1078774 You can control the number of lines in a port by the parameter port width.  You also have the option of not reconfiguring the port as an output port with each iteration of the VI by setting the iteration control to a non-zero value.
1079008 Port Width for the Lab boards, SCXI-1200, DAQBox-1200, DIO-24, DIO-32F, DIO-96, and AT-MIO-16D ports 2, 3 and 4 should be at least 8.

1084671 yudevice is the device number you assigned to the plug-in DAQ board during configuration. This parameter defaults to 1.
1084793 &port width is the total width in bits of the port. For example, you can combine two 4bit ports into an 8-bit port on an MIO board by setting port width to 8. 
1084953 When port width is greater than the physical width of a digital port, the following restrictions apply. The port width must be an integral multiple of the physical port width, and the port numbers in the combined port must begin with the port named by port number and must increase consecutively. For example, if port number is 3 and port width is 24 (bits), the VI uses ports 3, 4, and 5. 
1085346 (U32) pattern: contains the binary data to write to the port. Bit zero is the least significant bit for the port specified by the port number control. 
1085500 M(i32) iteration: controls when the VI performs initialization.  If iteration is 0, the VI configures the port for output and then writes the data.  If iteration is greater than zero, the VI assumes that configuration has already been done and simply writes the data.  You usually wire this input from a While loop iteration terminal.
1085837 )port number specifies the port this VI configures. A port number value of 0 signifies port 0, a port number of 1 signifies port 1, and so on. If you use a digital SCXI module, use the SCx!MDy!0 syntax, where x is the chassis ID and y is the module device number, to specify the port on a module.

1110855 $yudevice is the device number you assigned to the plug-in DAQ board during configuration. This parameter defaults to 1.
1110978 =port width is the total width in bits or the number of lines of the port. For example, you can combine two 4bit ports into an 8-bit port on an MIO board by setting port width to 8. 
1111161 When port width is greater than the physical width of a digital port, the following restrictions apply. The port width must be an integral multiple of the physical port width, and the port numbers in the combined port must begin with the port named by port number and must increase consecutively. For example, if port number is 3 and port width is 24 (bits), the VI uses ports 3, 4, and 5. 
1111554 (U32) pattern: contains the binary data read from the port. Bit zero is the least significant bit from the port specified by the port number control. 
1111707 J(i32) iteration: controls when the VI performs initialization.  If iteration is 0, the VI configures the port for input and then reads the data.  If iteration is greater than zero, the VI assumes that configuration has already been done and simply reads the data.  You usually wire this input from a While loop iteration terminal.
1112041 )port number specifies the port this VI configures. A port number value of 0 signifies port 0, a port number of 1 signifies port 1, and so on. If you use a digital SCXI module, use the SCx!MDy!0 syntax, where x is the chassis ID and y is the module device number, to specify the port on a module.

1126367 Most applications need only connect wires to the controls and indicators displayed in bold.  Connections to other controls and indicators are useful only if specifically needed.
1126546 The Read from Digital Port VI reads a user configured digital port.  The reading is displayed as a binary number in [pattern].
1126674 You have the option to not reconfigure the port as an input port by setting the iteration control to a non-zero value. You can also concatenate multiple ports to operate as one large port by using the port width paramter.
1126897 Port Width for the Lab boards, SCXI-1200, DAQBox-1200, DIO-24, DIO-32F, DIO-96, and AT-MIO-16D ports 2, 3 and 4 should be at least 8.
